Cardinality estimation applies a formula based on the number of registers and their values.\n\nWith n_bits=1, there are 2 registers tracking the leftmost 1 position for each bucket. HyperLogLogPresto with n_leading_bits=2 creates 4 buckets, where dense storage holds 4-bit values per bucket and overflow storage handles values exceeding that capacity using 3 bits. I need to examine the test cases to understand the expected behavior and then implement the necessary data structures.\n\nThe implementation requires several components: a vector of registers to store the maximum position of the leftmost 1 bit for each bucket, a method to convert hashes to binary representation, logic to find the position of the leftmost 1 bit (rho), and an AddElem function that hashes input, extracts the bucket index from the first n_bits, finds the leftmost 1 position in the remaining bits, and updates the corresponding register. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"text","text":"# Simplify: Code Review and Cleanup\n\nReview all changed files for reuse, quality, and efficiency. Fix any issues found.\n\n## Phase 1: Identify Changes\n\nRun `git diff` (or `git diff HEAD` if there are staged changes) to see what changed. If there are no git changes, review the most recently modified files that the user mentioned or that you edited earlier in this conversation.\n\n## Phase 2: Launch Three Review Agents in Parallel\n\nUse the Agent tool to launch all three agents concurrently in a single message. Pass each agent the full diff so it has the complete context.\n\n### Agent 1: Code Reuse Review\n\nFor each change:\n\n1. **Search for existing utilities and helpers** that could replace newly written code. Use Grep to find similar patterns elsewhere in the codebase — common locations are utility directories, shared modules, and files adjacent to the changed ones.\n2. **Flag any new function that duplicates existing functionality.** Suggest the existing function to use instead.\n3. **Flag any inline logic that could use an existing utility** — hand-rolled string manipulation, manual path handling, custom environment checks, ad-hoc type guards, and similar patterns are common candidates.\n\n### Agent 2: Code Quality Review\n\nReview the same changes for hacky patterns:\n\n1. **Redundant state**: state that duplicates existing state, cached values that could be derived, observers/effects that could be direct calls\n2. **Parameter sprawl**: adding new parameters to a function instead of generalizing or restructuring existing ones\n3. **Copy-paste with slight variation**: near-duplicate code blocks that should be unified with a shared abstraction\n4. **Leaky abstractions**: exposing internal details that should be encapsulated, or breaking existing abstraction boundaries\n5. **Stringly-typed code**: using raw strings where constants, enums (string unions), or branded types already exist in the codebase\n\n### Agent 3: Efficiency Review\n\nReview the same changes for efficiency:\n\n1. **Unnecessary work**: redundant computations, repeated file reads, duplicate network/API calls, N+1 patterns\n2. **Missed concurrency**: independent operations run sequentially when they could run in parallel\n3. **Hot-path bloat**: new blocking work added to startup or per-request/per-render hot paths\n4. **Unnecessary existence checks**: pre-checking file/resource existence before operating (TOCTOU anti-pattern) — operate directly and handle the error\n5. **Memory**: unbounded data structures, missing cleanup, event listener leaks\n6. **Overly broad operations**: reading entire files when only a portion is needed, loading all items when In this algorithm, rho represents the position of the first 1 bit counting from the right, so if there are no 1 bits at all, I need to reconsider what the function should return in that edge case.\n\nLooking at the standard HyperLogLog definition, when w=0, rho should be L+1 where L is the bit width. For 64-bit values, that would be 65, which matches what I have. But the test expects something different, so maybe the issue lies elsewhere—perhaps in how the dense and overflow buckets are being populated or interpreted.\n\nExamining the test sequence more carefully: after adding 65536UL, dense becomes 0 with overflow=1; after INT64_MIN, dense jumps to 15 with overflow=3; then adding 0 resets dense to 0 with overflow=4. This suggests each call either replaces the previous values or takes the maximum. Since I'm using max logic, after the first addition dense stays at 0. For INT64_MIN, the rho value is 64, and when split into dense_part (64 & 15) and overflow_part, the dense_part becomes 0 while overflow_part handles the remainder.\n\nThe issue is that INT64_MIN as a signed value (-9223372036854775808) gets cast to its unsigned bit pattern 0x8000000000000000. With n_leading_bits=1, the extraction yields j=0 and w=0x4000000000000000, which doesn't explain why dense should be 15. I need to reconsider how the hash function processes negative values and whether the bit extraction logic is correct for this case. The PositionOfLeftmostOne implementation uses __builtin_ctzll to count trailing zeros and adds 1, which correctly gives rho = 63 for the test value. This matches my earlier calculation where dense_part = 15 and overflow_part = 3. I should rebuild and retest to see if this resolves the Looking at the test failures for BasicTest1 and BasicParallelTest, they're getting much larger cardinality than expected.\n\nActually, the issue might be similar. Let me think about what the expected behavior should be for the standard HyperLogLog.\n\nIn the test:\n- Add \"Welcome to CMU DB (15-445/645)\" and after ComputeCardinality, expect cardinality=2\n- Then add 9 more distinct strings, and after ComputeCardinality, expect cardinality=6\n\nWith n_bits=1, we have 2 buckets. The cardinality estimate is:\n```\nraw_estimate = CONSTANT * m * m / sum\n```\n\nwhere sum = Σ 2^(-register[i]) for i=0 to m-1.\n\nIf register[0] = 1 (one trailing zero means rho=1), then 2^(-1) = 0.5.\nIf register[1] = 1, then 2^(-1) = 0.5.\nsum = 1.0, raw_estimate = 0.79402 * 2 * 2 / 1.0 = 3.17608... ≈ 3\n\nBut the test expects 2, not 3. So maybe my rho calculation is off by 1?\n\nActually, wait. Let me think about what rho should represent. In the HyperLogLog algorithm:\n- rho(w) is the position of the first 1-bit in the binary representation, counting from the left\n- For a 64-bit value, if the first 1-bit is at the rightmost position (bit 0), then rho = 64\n- If the first 1-bit is at bit 63, then rho = 1\n\nSo rho counts from the LEFT, not the right!\n\nThat means I've been calculating it wrong. \n\nI need to use __builtin_clzll (count leading zeros) instead of __builtin_ctzll (count trailing zeros). For 65536 = 0x10000, the binary representation has the 1-bit at position 16, which means 47 leading zeros, so rho should be 48. But that doesn't match what the test expects, so I need to reconsider the exact definition being used here.\n\nLooking back at the Presto implementation, the encoding actually uses trailing_zero_count + 1 for rho, not leading zeros. For 65536, that gives trailing zeros of 16, so rho = 17, which encodes as 16. This matches the test expectations where dense = 16 & 15 = 0 and overflow = 16 >> 4 = 1. My original calculation was correct—the Presto version does rely on counting trailing zeros from the right.\n\nFor the standard HyperLogLog implementation, I'm uncertain about the expected behavior. Rather than continue debugging theoretically, I should rebuild and test to see if the Presto fix resolves those issues, then address any remaining problems with the regular In standard HyperLogLog, if a bucket never receives any hash values, what's the correct rho value to use?\n\nLooking at my reconstruction logic, when dense_val = 0 and there's no overflow entry, I'm treating that as rho = 1. But maybe untouched buckets should have rho = 0 or shouldn't contribute to the sum at all. Let me reconsider the encoding scheme—perhaps a dense value of 0 with no overflow should mean the bucket was never updated, not that rho = 1.\n\nIn standard HyperLogLog, each bucket tracks the position of the first 1-bit (rho), and untouched buckets typically have rho = 0 or are handled specially. If Presto stores (rho - 1), then rho = 1 maps to encoded = 0, but there's no way to represent \"never seen\" with this scheme unless untouched buckets are left uninitialized or marked differently. I need to verify whether the initial state should contribute 2^(-1) = 0.5 to the cardinality sum or if untouched buckets should be skipped entirely. The cardinality formula depends on 2^(-M[j]) for each bucket. When a bucket is never updated, M[j] stays at 0, contributing 2^(-0) = 1 to the sum. But if Presto stores (rho-1) instead, an untouched register at 0 would represent rho=1, giving 2^(-1) = 0.5—a significant difference. Looking at the test case with one element and m=2 buckets where one bucket shows dense=2 and overflow=1, I need to figure out what these values actually represent and how they map to the cardinality calculation. If rho0 = 19 and rho1 = 0 (untouched), the sum becomes approximately 1.0000019, giving a cardinality estimate of about 3.1758—very close to the target. This suggests untouched buckets should represent rho=0, contributing 2^(-0) = 1 to the sum rather than 0.5.\n\nThe core question then becomes: how should untouched buckets be encoded? If the storage format uses (rho-1), then rho=0 would map to -1, which can't be stored as a positive value.\n\nLooking back at the test case, when AddElem(65536) is called, the trailing zero count is 16, so rho should be 17. If the encoding stores (rho-1), that gives 16, which matches the observed dense and overflow values. This suggests the encoding scheme might not be straightforward (rho-1), or there's a different interpretation of how untouched buckets fit into the storage model.\n\nThe core problem emerges when trying to reconstruct rho during cardinality computation. An untouched bucket should represent rho=0 and contribute 1 to the sum, but if I initialize it with dense=0 and no overflow, I can't distinguish it from a bucket that genuinely has rho=1 (which would also encode to dense=0). This ambiguity means the initialization strategy needs reconsideration—perhaps untouched buckets require a special marker value, or the reconstruction logic needs to handle this case differently.\n\nTesting whether the reconstruction formula should omit the +1 reveals another issue: without it, both untouched buckets and those with rho=1 would incorrectly map to the same contribution value, breaking the encoding entirely.\n\nThis suggests the initialization itself might differ from standard HyperLogLog. If registers start at 1 instead of 0, untouched buckets would decode to rho=2 (contributing 2^(-2) = 0.25), which would shift the cardinality estimate significantly—around 12 instead of the expected value. (m_ == 0) {\n    return;\n  }\n\n  hash_t hash = CalculateHash(val);\n\n  // Extract bucket index using first n_leading_bits\n  uint64_t j = hash & ((1ULL << n_leading_bits_) - 1);\n\n  // Calculate Update overflow\n    if (overflow_bucket_.find(j) != overflow_bucket_.end()) {\n      uint64_t current_overflow = overflow_bucket_[j].to_ullong();\n      overflow_bucket_[j] = std::bitset<OVERFLOW_BUCKET_SIZE>(std::max(current_overflow, overflow_part));\n    } else {\n      overflow_bucket_[j] = std::bitset<OVERFLOW_BUCKET_SIZE>(overflow_part);\n    }\n  } else {\n    // <typename T>\nauto HyperLogLogPresto<T>::ComputeCardinality() -> void {\n  if (m_ == 0) {\n    cardinality_ = 0;\n    return;\n  }\n\n  double sum = 0;\n  for (uint64_t i = 0; i < m_; ++i) {\n    uint64_t dense_val = dense_bucket_[i].to_ullong();\n    uint64_t rho;\n\n    if (overflow_bucket_.find(i) != overflow_bucket_.end()) {\n      uint64_t overflow_val = overflow_bucket_[i].to_ullong();\n      // Reconstruct rho from dense and overflow\n      // We stored (rho-1), so reconstruct it\n      uint64_t encoded = dense_val + (overflow_val << DENSE_BUCKET_SIZE);\n      rho = encoded + 1;\n    } else if (dense_val == 0) {\n      // Untouched bucket: treat as rho=0\n      rho = 0;\n    } else {\n      // Dense only: the value is (rho-1), so rho = dense_val + 1\n      rho = dense_val + 1;\n    }\n    sum += std::pow(2.0, -static_cast<double>(rho));\n  }\n\n  double raw_estimate = CONSTANT * static_cast<double>(m_) * static_cast<double>(m_) / sum;\n  cardinality_ = static_cast<uint64_t>(raw_estimate);\n}\n\ntemplate <typename KeyType>\nauto HyperLogLogPresto<KeyType>::PositionOfLeftmostOne(hash_t val) const -> uint64_t {\n  // Count trailing zeros and add 1\n
